Reminds me of one time I got lost in an amusement park. There was a big enclosed attraction where you can fire foam balls at people. Like there were all sorts of little airsoft turrets and sling shots set up and you just run around shooting each other. I went in with my dad and maybe one or some of my siblings (I honestly don't remember). For whatever reason, I decided it'd be a brilliant idea to go exploring, so I snuck away from my dad and left the attraction. I got outside, checked out the pretty flowers in this raised garden patch, and figured I should go back in and find him. I walked back into the attraction through the exit, glanced around at this big room with a bunch of colorful balls flying everywhere, and couldn't see him. So small-child-me concluded he must have already left. In a panic, I left the attraction again and circled it to see if I could find him. Nope. Nothing. At that point, I sat on the stone fence that lined the flower beds outside the attraction and just started sobbing. It was only then that a park employee appeared and asked me where my parents were. When I told them I didn't know, they then asked the very logical question "What's your parents' names?" so that they could call them on the intercom. I remember this bit vividly. Between tears, I told this employee, "I'm not allowed to say my mom's name but my dad's name is [full name]." So then the employee calls my dad on the intercom, and it turned out he was still inside the attraction all along and I'd missed him. He was confused, my mom showed up also confused, and I was mega embarrassed but relieved to be back with them. To this day, I have no idea how I was even able to sneak away like that. the funny thing is, while other kids said they would ride away i practically did it. it was spring break for me in i think 3rd or 4th grade. My mom and our roommate were at work and my younger and older sister got in a fight against me. We were fighting while playing outside so after we argued they ran inside and locked me out. we all didnt have phones at the time so i just continued playing without them while being locked out. i heard my sister call my name to the back door so i assumed she was gonna let me back in. I waked over to the back door to see a note, 2 dollars, and my shoes. The note saying "go away we dont want you anymore, mom wont miss you either!"  and instead of being sad or angry i was kinda excited. I dont know why i was excited maybe i thought that i was going on some adventure idk. I put on my shoes, took the money and started walking down our street and around our neighbor hood. After walking for about 2 hours and playing with the stray dogs i got hungry. My friend lived about two blocks away from me and i decided to go to her house and ask her dad if i could live with him. I walked for about 30 minutes before seeing a car that looked vaguely similar one to the car my mom and our roommate drove to work, Which was a yellow-goldish Honda van. I didnt think anything of it but as it got closer to me while i was walking i started hearing yelling that sounded like my mom but i didnt know where it was coming from. Until the car pulled up to me. Turns out my mom and roommate left work early and were driving to see my moms daughter wearing a blue ninja turtle shirt, yellow tie-dye shorts, and purple sandals. I was obviously in trouble before i showed them the note and told my mom what my sisters did. My mom busted into the house and after i heard children screaming, shoes being thrown, and the sound of spanking i got McDonalds with our roommate. Im generally surprised no one called CPS with all the bloody murder screams. I dont know if any of my family members remember this but i remember every second of this event in my child hood. XD

Hilarious story!!! My running away story wasn't like this, though. I ran away from home the summer before my senior year of high school. Here's what happened...   So both parents were/are abusive in multiple ways and I just couldn't take it anymore. My dad was living in Florida at the time and when it was time to fly there, I packed as much as I could into a duffle bag, suitcase, and my purse. On my way back "home," I dodged my mom and stepfather at the airport and my friend picked me up and we left for her house. This ended in a really rough and messy falling-out which led to getting kicked out of my friend's house for becoming the monster I was running away from. I lost myself for a while and was figuring out how to navigate school while homeless. But thanks to the power of going from house to house, homeless shelters, locker rooms, and city benches, I was still able to do my homework!  So I graduated high school out of spite and invited my parents because I knew they didn't believe I could do it. And boy, was I correct... The incubator told me right after the ceremony that she and my stepdad had a bet going that I either wasn't going to graduate or was gonna graduate pregnant... while my dad decided it would be cute and quirky to throw a fit because I finally stood up to him and made it clear that I was done taking his narcissism crap. Safe to say, I haven't spoken to them in 4 years and I'm much better off now. Still healing, but yeah.  This isn't an encouragement for people to run away from home, by the way. I lost all my friends and family, lost myself completely and became a really awful person until reaching rock bottom. A lot of traumatic stuff happened that has left deep wounds that will take many years to be healed. In hindsight, I probably should have just waited or called CPS or something because I would've been much better off. But it's my story and I get to decide how it ends.

I never thought of running away, but accidentally freaked my mom out one time when I was six.  I was in my room. My bed at that time was what they called a "captain's bed." It was high off the floor with a cabinet, some drawers and shelves on one side. Sort of like a bed on top of a dresser.  I was reading comics and one of them slid into the gap between the bed and the wall.  Annoyed, I climbed down and pushed the bed away from the wall. I saw the comic, some small toys and a coloring book that had gone missing. I pushed the bed far enough out that I could squeeze behind it and get my stuff. That's when I realized how roomy the cavity under the bed was. The storage part was only about a third as wide as the bed and there was like a whole secret room behind it.  I grabbed my pillow, flashlight & the rest of my comics and went back under the bed into my new clubhouse.  My mom, who had been doing housework, peeked into my room to check on me. Not seeing me in there, she thought I must have gone outside to play. When she couldn't find me in the backyard, she started panicking. She went over to the neighbors' houses to see if I was playing with their kids. When she couldn't find me, the other neighborhood moms started freaking out, too.  I faintly heard my name being called outside. Confused, I crawled out from behind my bed and went out to see what was going on.  Mom was standing  in the front yard  with her back to the house calling for me. I could hear other ladies up and down the street calling, too. I came up behind her and said, "Momma?"  She was relieved and angry at the same time. After everyone settled down and figured out what had happened, we all went back inside.  When dad got home from work, mom, exasperated, told him what had happened. When he laughed about it, she got really mad at him.

Okay, here's how I almost ran away:   When I was about 6 or 7 maybe 5, I used to take my bike out and ride around our local rec center. On one of these nights while I was biking in circles I just randomly decided to keep going forward rather then turning back around. For no reason mind you. I just felt like running away and wanted to see what would happen. I went over the bridge, past our local willow tree, and on to the sidewalk next to the street. I got to about Dixie road (look it up on google maps if you'd like) when some random women in a car stopped near me and asked me "where are you going?"   I tried to think of an excuse like "My parents walked very far ahead and I couldn't catch up," or some bull crap like that, but I think all I said was "I got lost." She ended up calling the police and they took me home to some not really angry, just curious folks asking why I would do such a thing. My big brain excuse as to how I ran away was "some gang bangers chased me! I got away from them, but got lost while trying to escape."  This was a lie as I fully knew how to get home from where I was. I just had to turn around. My parents actually believed me surprisingly and didn't punish me or anything after that. When I got home my sisters hugged me very hard and I went back to watching Thomas music videos on my tablet until I went to bed. Years later I told them the truth and they didn't really care since that was so long ago. So yeah, that's how I almost ran away from home.

I CAME AS FAST AS I COULD!
I remember my own "running away" story like it was yesterday. My parents and I had a fight, so I decided "I'm leaving!" and they just let me, under the assumption I wouldn't take it seriously. I made it as far as my neighbor's house and just sat on their porch to wait for the school bus (which I thought was a normal city bus and would just take me anywhere I wanted for free. I had no grasp on the financial system of the U.S at the time). Eventually, I got bored and crawled into their bushes to take a nap. When I woke up, there was a flashlight in my face and it was 11:15 PM. Mom and Dad got freaked out when I didn't come home and thought I actually followed through with my plan and ran off. I didn't get in as much trouble as I thought I would, mostly because they both gave me permission to, but they still guilt-tripped me into never doing it again by saying how much everyone would miss me if I left.

So, funny story, my mom and her siblings (younger set of twins, one boy and one girl) were in that exact home alone situation when they were younger. My mom was about 12-15 and my aunt and uncle were 7-8 years old. Like Rebecca, they decided to play this same prank on my grandparents. There was a shelf-like piece of stone above the door that was strong enough to hold up heavy boxes so my mom helped my aunt and uncle climb up there and hide themselves with the boxes. She also halfway opened the back door, hid their school backpacks, and messed up their closets. When my grandma came home first, my mom was in a fake panic and hysterically told her that her and her siblings had fought and when she went to take a break in her room and came back, they were gone. My mom gave off the idea that they had either run away or been kidnapped. My poor grandma wasn't as confident in her kids courage as Rebecca's, so of course she started sobbing and panicking alongside my mom. Right as she was about to call the police, my mom felt guilty for pranking her so bad (and also scared to actually call the police) and said "MOM IM KIDDING THEYRE FINE". Mind you, I've never seen my grandma very angry, only a couple times. But my mom said that the slow turn around her shoulder and the glare my grandma gave her _terrified_ her. Long story short, my mom revealed where my aunt and uncle were hiding, they all got into huge trouble (mostly my mom since it was her idea) and even now my grandma still gets grumpy about the story, but still amused. Yo
Baragon (ãƒãƒ©ã‚´ãƒ³ Baragon) is a subterranean reptile kaiju who first appeared in the 1965 Toho film Frankenstein vs. Baragon, and later debuted in the Godzilla series in the 1968 film Destroy All Monsters.  The original Baragon from Frankenstein vs. Baragon was a villainous creature that came to the surface to feed on livestock and people. As the creature only surfaced at night, most people blamed Frankenstein for the beast's attacks. When Baragon threatened Frankenstein's caretaker Sueko Togami, Frankenstein challenged him to battle, and successfully defeated him only to fall into a fissure caused by Baragon's burrowing. The second generation Baragon in Destroy All Monsters was living on the human-monitored Monsterland facility at the end of the 20th century, and disappeared after the Kilaaks invaded the island and took control of the monsters. Baragon later appeared at Mount Fuji and witnessed the battle between the Earth monsters and King Ghidorah after the aliens' mind control was severed. Baragon's next film appearance came in the Millennium series film Godzilla, Mothra and King Ghidorah: Giant Monsters All-Out Attack, where he was the first of the three Guardian Monsters to battle Godzilla. While not as popular as monsters like Mothra or King Ghidorah, Baragon has maintained a strong fan following over the years.

Oddly enough I ran home instead of running away. Mainly because all my stuff was there and I was in the countryside so it would take at least a 5-mile walk into town. I forgot what my parents went to school for but they left me on the playground and thought "eh he'll be fine" and for the most part, I was. Until dark and I was starting to get nervous that my parents weren't going to pick me up. So I looked for the car where we parked and It's gone. My childhood trauma of being left alone set in and I started walking home (I knew the general route to my house). About give or take 2 miles in a truck pulls up, I get in because I recognized them as my neighbors and I told them my address and they drove me in the opposite direction.
